                                                                                            <span class="kicker-label"><a href="https://www.nytimes.com/pages/politics/index.html">Politics</a></span>
                                                                                                                                                                    </h3>
                        			<h1 itemprop="headline" id="headline" class="headline">Health Secretary Tom Price Resigns After Drawing Ire for Chartered Flights</h1>
	                                                <div id="story-meta-footer" class="story-meta-footer">
                                                                                                    

<p class="byline-dateline"><span class="byline" itemprop="author creator" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person"  itemid="https://www.nytimes.com/by/peter-baker">By <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/by/peter-baker" title="More Articles by PETER BAKER"><span class="byline-author" data-byline-name="PETER BAKER" itemprop="name" data-twitter-handle="peterbakernyt">PETER BAKER</span></a>, </span><span class="byline" itemprop="author creator" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person"  itemid="https://www.nytimes.com/by/glenn-thrush"><a href="https://www.nytimes.com/by/glenn-thrush" title="More Articles by GLENN THRUSH"><span class="byline-author" data-byline-name="GLENN THRUSH" itemprop="name" data-twitter-handle="GlennThrush">GLENN THRUSH</span></a> and </span><span class="byline" itemprop="author creator" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person"  itemid="https://www.nytimes.com/by/maggie-haberman"><a href="https://www.nytimes.com/by/maggie-haberman" title="More Articles by MAGGIE HABERMAN"><span class="byline-author" data-byline-name="MAGGIE HABERMAN" itemprop="name" data-twitter-handle="maggieNYT">MAGGIE HABERMAN</span></a></span><time class="dateline" datetime="2017-09-30T00:55:11-04:00" itemprop="dateModified" content="2017-09-30T00:55:11-04:00">SEPT. 29, 2017</time>
</p>

                                    <div class="story-meta-footer-sharetools">
                        <div id="sharetools-story-meta-footer" aria-label="tools" role="group" class="sharetools theme-classic  sharetools-story-meta-footer  "
data-shares="facebook,twitter,email,show-all,save"

	data-publish-date="September 29, 2017"

    <div class="story-body-supplemental">
    <div class="story-body story-body-1">
        <figure class="promo media video lede layout-large-horizontal "
    data-videoid="100000005468371"

    <figcaption class="caption">
        <h4 class="headline">Tom Price Resigns Under Pressure</h4>

        <div class="caption-video">
            <div class="summary-credit">
                <p class="summary">Tom Price, the health and human services secretary, resigned on Friday. Mr. Price drew criticism for his use of expensive chartered flights, which undermined President Trump’s promise to “drain the swamp” of an entitled capital.</p>
                <span class="credit video-credit" itemprop="copyrightHolder">
                    By CHRIS CIRILLO, GLENN THRUSH and A.J. CHAVAR on                                                                <span class="visually-hidden">Publish Date </span>September 29, 2017.
                                    </span>
                <span class="credit photo-credit" itemprop="copyrightHolder">
                    Photo by Gabriella Demczuk for The New York Times.
                </span>
                                    <a class="video-link" href= https://www.nytimes.com/video/us/politics/100000005468371/tom-price-resigns-trump.html?action=click&amp;contentCollection=us&amp;module=lede&amp;region=caption&amp;pgtype=article >Watch in Times Video &#187;</a>
                            </div>

            <div class="sharetools-video-container">
                                <div id="sharetools-video-tools-100000005468371"
                    class="sharetools sharetools-video-tools">
                    <ul>
                        <li class="sharetool embed-sharetool">
                            <a href="javascript:;" data-share="embed" data-modal-title="">
                                <i class="icon sprite-icon"></i>
                                <span class="sharetool-text ">embed</span>
                            </a>
                        </li>
                    </ul>
                </div>
                                <div id="sharetools-video-inline-100000005468371"
                    class="sharetools sharetools-video-inline"
                    data-shares="facebook|,twitter|"
                    data-url="https://www.nytimes.com/video/us/politics/100000005468371/tom-price-resigns-trump.html?action=click&amp;contentCollection=us&amp;module=lede&amp;region=caption&amp;pgtype=article"
                    data-title="Tom Price Resigns Under Pressure"
                    data-description="Tom Price, the health and human services secretary, resigned on Friday. Mr. Price drew criticism for his use of expensive chartered flights, which undermined President Trump’s promise to “drain the swamp” of an entitled capital."
                    data-content-type="video">
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
    </figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="271" data-total-count="271">WASHINGTON — Tom Price, the health and human services secretary, resigned under pressure on Friday after racking up at least $400,000 in travel bills for chartered flights and undermining President Trump’s promise to drain the swamp of a corrupt and entitled capital.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="373" data-total-count="644">Already in trouble with Mr. Trump for months of <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/26/us/politics/mcconnell-obamacare-repeal-graham-cassidy-trump.html?mcubz=1">unsuccessful efforts</a> to repeal and replace President Barack Obama’s health care program, Mr. Price failed to defuse the president’s anger by offering regret and a partial reimbursement. His departure was the latest from an administration buffeted by turbulence at the top, and capped a week of setbacks for the president.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="438" data-total-count="1082">“I’m not happy, O.K.?” Mr. Trump told reporters who asked about Mr. Price as the president prepared to leave for his New Jersey golf club for the weekend, barely an hour before the resignation was announced. “I can tell you, I’m not happy.” He called Mr. Price “a very good man” but added that the secretary’s offer to pay back the government for just part of the cost of the private flights “would be unacceptable.”</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="492" data-total-count="1574">Mr. Price ran afoul of one of the president’s most consequential campaign pledges. While some of Mr. Trump’s advisers privately make light of his vow to drain the swamp of Washington privilege, to many of his voters, it was a threshold promise. The firestorm over Mr. Price came as the president was already on the defensive with his base, as the incumbent mainstream Republican senator he backed in an Alabama primary race <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/26/us/politics/roy-moore-alabama-senate.html">lost to an insurgent</a> channeling Mr. Trump’s election movement.</p><div id="story-ad-1" class="story-ad ad ad-placeholder nocontent robots-nocontent ">
    <div class="accessibility-ad-header visually-hidden">
    <p>Advertisement</p>
</div>
<a class="visually-hidden skip-to-text-link" href="#story-continues-1">Continue reading the main story</a>
</div>
<p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="325" data-total-count="1899" id="story-continues-1">“It’s hard to see how a cabinet secretary can drain the swamp from 42,000 feet in the plush interior of a taxpayer-funded Gulfstream 4,” said Laura Ingraham, a conservative talk show host and Trump supporter who, like others, defied the president by backing Roy Moore, the insurgent Senate candidate who won in Alabama.</p>        <a class="visually-hidden skip-to-text-link" href="#story-continues-2">Continue reading the main story</a>
    </div><!-- close story-body -->
    <div class="supplemental first" id="supplemental-1">
    </div><!-- close supplemental -->
</div><!-- close story-body-supplemental -->
<div class="story-interrupter" id="story-continues-2">
    <div id="FlexAd" class="ad flex-ad nocontent robots-nocontent">
    <div class="accessibility-ad-header visually-hidden">
    <p>Advertisement</p>
</div>
<a class="visually-hidden skip-to-text-link" href="#story-continues-3">Continue reading the main story</a>
    <div class="flex-ad-creative"></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="story-body-supplemental">
    <div class="story-body story-body-2">
        <p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="256" data-total-count="2155" id="story-continues-3">Mr. Trump berated Mr. Price in the Oval Office on Friday afternoon for about two hours before heading out to meet with reporters, according to people informed about the meeting. All cabinet travel requests now must be cleared by the White House, they said.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="221" data-total-count="2376">The White House’s <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/the-press-office/2017/09/29/statement-press-secretary">announcement of Mr. Price’s departure was sparse</a>, with none of the customary thanks for his service; it said simply that he had “offered his resignation earlier today and the president accepted.”</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="399" data-total-count="2775">In his resignation letter to Mr. Trump, Mr. Price said: “I have spent 40 years both as a doctor and public servant putting people first. I regret that the recent events have created a distraction from these important objectives. Success on these issues is more important than any one person. In order for you to move forward without further disruption, I am officially tendering my resignation.”</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="376" data-total-count="3151">Mr. Trump tapped Don J. Wright, a deputy assistant secretary for health and the director of the Office of Disease Prevention and Health Promotion, to serve as acting secretary. Possible candidates for a successor include Seema Verma, the administrator of the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services, and Scott Gottlieb, the commissioner of the Food and Drug Administration.</p> <figure id="document-Read-the-Resignation-Letter-Tom-Price-Sent-to" class="interactive promo  layout-large">
        <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2017/09/29/us/politics/document-Read-the-Resignation-Letter-Tom-Price-Sent-to.html">
                <figcaption class="interactive-caption">
                        <h3 class="interactive-kicker">
                Document            </h3>
                        <h2 class="interactive-headline">
                Read the Resignation Letter Tom Price Sent to President Trump            </h2>
            <p class="interactive-summary">
                Tom Price sent a letter on Friday to President Trump resigning as health secretary. Mr. Price had been under pressure after racking up at least $400,000 in travel bills, footed by the taxpayers, for chartered flights.            </p>
        </figcaption>
        
        <div class="interactive-image-container">
            <div class="interactive-image">
                <img src="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2017/09/29/us/politics/image-Read-the-Resignation-Letter-Tom-Price-Sent-to/image-Read-the-Resignation-Letter-Tom-Price-Sent-to-master495.gif" />
            </div>
            <div class="interactive-overlay">
                <i class="icon sprite-icon interactive-overlay-icon"></i>
                                <span class="interactive-overlay-text">
                    OPEN Document                </span>
                            </div>
        </div>

            </a>
</figure>
<p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="459" data-total-count="3610">Mr. Price’s job was on the line since the <a href="http://www.politico.com/story/2017/09/19/tom-price-chartered-planes-flights-242908">first</a> of a <a href="http://www.politico.com/story/2017/09/21/tom-price-private-charter-plane-flights-242989">string</a> of <a href="http://www.politico.com/story/2017/09/23/tom-price-private-jet-travel-review-hhs-243057">reports</a> by Politico, on Sept. 19, about his extensive use of chartered aircraft. The president has fumed privately and publicly about Mr. Price’s actions. Hoping to assuage Mr. Trump, the secretary <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/28/us/politics/tom-price-chartered-flights.html">offered on Thursday</a> to reimburse the government $51,887 — which he said represented the cost of his seat on the trips — of the at least $400,000 spent. But it was not enough to save his job.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="287" data-total-count="3897">Mr. Price, a physician and a former Republican congressman from Georgia who had long opposed Mr. Obama’s Affordable Care Act, served as a point man on Mr. Trump’s drive to scrap the law. In July, Mr. Trump said he would fire Mr. Price if he did not get the votes for the legislation.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="136" data-total-count="4033">“He better get them,” Mr. Trump <a href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/the-press-office/2017/07/24/remarks-president-trump-2017-national-scout-jamboree">told an audience</a> with Mr. Price at his side. “Otherwise, I’ll say, ‘Tom, you’re fired.’”</p><div id="story-ad-2" class="story-ad ad ad-placeholder nocontent robots-nocontent ">
    <div class="accessibility-ad-header visually-hidden">
    <p>Advertisement</p>
</div>
<a class="visually-hidden skip-to-text-link" href="#story-continues-4">Continue reading the main story</a>
</div>
<p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="361" data-total-count="4394" id="story-continues-4">He said it in a jocular fashion, and his audience took it as a jest, but in fact the president has been privately simmering about Mr. Price over the unsuccessful efforts to pass health care legislation in the Senate. While a bill passed the House, the <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2017/09/26/us/politics/mcconnell-obamacare-repeal-graham-cassidy-trump.html?mcubz=1">latest effort collapsed</a> this week when enough Senate Republicans defected to deprive Mr. Trump of a majority.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="428" data-total-count="4822">Mr. Price had been under fire from the start. During his confirmation hearing in January, Senate Democrats pressed him on the more than $100,000 in pharmaceutical and medical stocks he owned. Democrats said that Mr. Price had understated the value of his 400,613 shares in an Australian company, Innate Immunotherapeutics. He defended himself, saying, “Everything that I did was ethical, above board, legal and transparent.”</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="305" data-total-count="5127">In just eight months since taking office, Mr. Trump has fired or lost a chief of staff, a chief strategist, a national security adviser, a press secretary, two communications directors, a deputy chief of staff, a deputy national security adviser, the F.B.I. director and numerous other aides and advisers.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="305" data-total-count="5432">Mr. Price may not be the only senior official to face anger over travel bills. In recent days, a slew of reports about the fast-lane habits of the cabinet have resulted in a mounting public relations headache for the Trump administration, which is stocked by billionaires accustomed to using private jets.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="491" data-total-count="5923">Ryan Zinke, the interior secretary, used a chartered airplane for several flights, including a $12,000 trip to deliver a speech celebrating a new professional hockey team in Las Vegas. Scott Pruitt, the administrator of the Environmental Protection Agency, has spent more than $58,000 on chartered and military flights, and David Shulkin, the veterans affairs secretary, took his wife on a <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/investigations/va-chief-took-in-wimbledon-river-cruise-on-european-work-trip/2017/09/29/c1f17046-a458-11e7-8c37-e1d99ad6aa22_story.html?utm_term=.0143d9b26a06">10-day trip to Europe</a> that mixed business meetings and sightseeing, <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/energy-environment/wp/2017/09/27/epas-pruitt-took-charter-military-flights-that-cost-taxpayers-more-than-58000/?utm_term=.1cb7ec2c7eac">according to The Washington Post</a>.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="286" data-total-count="6209">Treasury Secretary Steven Mnuchin asked about using a $25,000-an-hour military plane for his European honeymoon and later used a government jet to fly to Fort Knox in Kentucky in August, a trip that offered him a clear view of a solar eclipse, although he later disclaimed any interest.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="469" data-total-count="6678">Other cabinet members issued statements explaining their travel practices. The Small Business Administration said its chief, Linda McMahon, had used private air services and that “on the rare occasion” she had, she “covered the entire cost out of her own pocket.” Betsy DeVos, the education secretary, travels on personally owned aircraft “at zero cost to U.S. taxpayers” because she “neither seeks, nor accepts, any reimbursement,” the department said.</p><div class="newsletter-signup variant-1-hidden " id="newsletter-promo" data-newsletter-productCode="NN" data-newsletter-productTitle="Morning Briefing" aria-labeledby="newsletter-promo-heading">
    <h2 class="visually-hidden" id="newsletter-promo-heading">Newsletter Sign Up</h2>

<div id="#continues-post-newsletter"></div>
<p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="248" data-total-count="6926">The sensitivity about the situation within the cabinet was clear on Friday when Mr. Zinke delivered an energy policy address to the Heritage Foundation. He opened his speech by lashing out at what he called “a little B.S.” on chartered flights.</p><div id="story-ad-3" class="story-ad ad ad-placeholder nocontent robots-nocontent ">
    <div class="accessibility-ad-header visually-hidden">
    <p>Advertisement</p>
</div>
<a class="visually-hidden skip-to-text-link" href="#story-continues-5">Continue reading the main story</a>
</div>
<p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="247" data-total-count="7173" id="story-continues-5">“I fly coach,” he said, adding that he uses chartered or military flights only when necessary. “Every time I travel, I submit the travel plans to the ethics department,” he added. “I will always be honest and up front about my travel.”</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="334" data-total-count="7507">Current and former West Wing officials said oversight of Mr. Trump’s cabinet was so lax in the past that Stephen K. Bannon, then the president’s chief strategist, requested meetings once every 60 days to review each member’s agenda and travel itinerary. The secretaries did not flag the questionable flights, the officials said.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="357" data-total-count="7864">John F. Kelly, the White House chief of staff who has tried to impose a military discipline on a chaotic West Wing with mixed success, has ordered the president’s budget director, Mick Mulvaney, to revamp the review process for flights and set limits on prices that cabinet members can pay for transportation, according to two people briefed on the plans.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="420" data-total-count="8284">At a recent meeting with legislative affairs aides for cabinet agencies, Marc Short, the White House legislative affairs director, warned that they should be prepared for additional reports on cabinet secretaries’ expenses, according to a person who attended. Mr. Short said that agencies should assume everything will be made public eventually — and urged the aides to come clean with the president’s staff first.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="599" data-total-count="8883">Additionally, Rick Dearborn, a deputy White House chief of staff tasked with overseeing the cabinet, has been in the president’s cross hairs, according to an aide familiar with the situation. Mr. Dearborn accompanied Mr. Trump on his visit to Alabama last week to support Senator Luther Strange, who lost to Mr. Moore in the state’s Republican primary. On the flight back to Washington, the president lashed out at Mr. Dearborn and White House political director Bill Stepien because he was left supporting a candidate who seemed likely to lose, said the aide who was not authorized to be named.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="211" data-total-count="9094">Two people on the plane insisted the president never chastised his aides. Another adviser said Mr. Dearborn and Mr. Stepien had both cautioned against the trip, but caught Mr. Trump’s wrath once it went badly.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="399" data-total-count="9493">Critics were unmollified by Mr. Price’s departure. “While his resignation ends his time in the government, it does not end the private jet scandal that others in the Trump administration, including Mnuchin, Pruitt and Zinke, find themselves in,” Noah Bookbinder, the executive director of Citizens for Responsibility and Ethics in Washington, a progressive watchdog group, said in a statement.</p><p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="142" data-total-count="9635">“This administration,” he added, “seems to believe that the government and the taxpayers serve them rather than the other way around.”</p><button class="button comments-button  theme-speech-bubble-large" data-skip-to-para-id="">
</button>
<p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="159" data-total-count="9794">Representative Joseph Crowley of New York, the chairman of the House Democratic Caucus, said the episode demonstrated a lack of judgment in the administration.</p><div id="story-ad-4" class="story-ad ad ad-placeholder nocontent robots-nocontent ">
    <div class="accessibility-ad-header visually-hidden">
    <p>Advertisement</p>
</div>
<a class="visually-hidden skip-to-text-link" href="#story-continues-6">Continue reading the main story</a>
</div>
<p class="story-body-text story-content" data-para-count="232" data-total-count="10026" id="story-continues-6">“President Trump talked a big game about draining the swamp, yet he continues to surround himself with staff and administration officials who behave as though a separate set of rules apply to them,” he said. “That must end.”</p><div id="addenda" class="addenda">
    <div class="story-addendum story-content theme-correction">
        <strong> Correction: September 29, 2017 </strong> <br/>
        <p>An earlier version of this article referred incorrectly to the events leading up to Secretary Price&rsquo;s resignation. It was President Trump, not former President Barack Obama, who threatened to fire Mr. Price.</p>    </div>
</div>

href="/videos/weather/2017/09/26/life-without-basic-needs-in-puerto-rico-orig-tc.cnn/video/playlists/puerto-rico/"  ><span class="cd__headline-text"> Life without basic needs in Puerto Rico</span><span class="cd__headline-icon"></span></a></h3></div></div></article></div></div></div></div></div></section></div><div class="pg-rail-tall__body" itemprop="articleBody"><section class="zn zn-body-text zn-body zn--idx-0 zn--ordinary zn-has-multiple-containers zn-has-47-containers" data-eq-pts="xsmall: 0, medium: 460, large: 780, full16x9: 1100" id="body-text" data-vr-zone="zone-1-0" data-zone-label="bodyText" data-containers="47" id="body-text" data-zn-id="body-text"><div class="l-container"><div class="el__leafmedia el__leafmedia--storyhighlights"><div class="el__storyhighlights_wrapper"><div class="el__storyhighlights"><h3 class="el__headline">Story highlights</h3><ul class="el__storyhighlights__list"><li class="el__storyhighlights__item el__storyhighlights--normal">San Juan mayor pushes for better federal response in getting supplies distributed</li><li class="el__storyhighlights__item el__storyhighlights--normal">National Weather Service has flash flood watch in effect until Sunday </li></ul></div><div class="ad ad--epic" data-ad-text="show"><div id="ad_ns_btf_01" class="ad-ad_ns_btf_01 ad-refresh-default"></div></div></div></div><div class="el__leafmedia el__leafmedia--sourced-paragraph"><p class="zn-body__paragraph speakable"><cite class="el-editorial-source"> (CNN)</cite>San Juan Mayor Carmen Yulín Cruz made her message clear on her black shirt that read: "Help Us, We Are Dying." </p></div><div class="zn-body__paragraph speakable">"People are drinking out of creeks here in San Juan," she told CNN's Anderson Cooper on Friday night. "You have people in buildings and they're becoming caged in their own buildings -- old people, retired people that don't have any electricity."</div><div class="ad ad--epic ad--mobile" data-ad-text="show"><div id="ad_rect_atf_02" class="ad-ad_rect_atf_02 ad-refresh-default"></div></div><ul class="cn cn-list-hierarchical-xs cn--idx-4 cn-zoneAdContainer"></ul><div class="zn-body__paragraph speakable">Ten days after Hurricane Maria rammed into Puerto Rico as a Category 4 storm,<strong> </strong>the US commonwealth is dealing with a humanitarian crisis as millions remain without electricity and water, and limited access to gas and cash. At least 16 people have died as a result of the storm, the government has said.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph">Already stricken with logistics, communications and supply issues, Puerto Rico is expected to see heavy rain this weekend that could further impede recovery efforts for its 3.4 million residents. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph">Some areas still remain flooded and now, Puerto Rico is under a <a href="http://forecast.weather.gov/product.php?site=NWS&issuedby=SJU&product=HWO" target="_blank">flash flood watch</a> until late Sunday because of the predicted rain, which could be between 2 and 4 inches each day, the National Weather Service said. Low-lying areas are at risk for flooding as water pumps aren't functioning at full capacity.</div><div class="el__embedded el__embedded--fullstandardwidth"><div class="el__gallery--fullstandardwidth js__gallery--fullstandardwidth js__leafmedia--gallery"><div class="el-carousel__wrapper"><div class=" js-owl-carousel owl-carousel carousel--full body" data-galleryname=" Hurricane Maria slams the Caribbean" data-cut-format="16:9" data-is-gallery="true" data-slide-count="36"><div data-slidename=" Hurricane Maria slams the Caribbean" data-analytics="_body_image"><div class="el__resize"><div class="el__position media js-gallery-aspect-ratio-wrapper"><img class="media__image media__image--responsive media__image--cut-format" alt="An apartment building is missing a wall in San Juan, Puerto Rico, on Monday, September 25, nearly a week after Hurricane Maria devastated the US commonwealth. class="zn-body__paragraph">• Military troops and disaster relief workers are improving supply chains, and "you'll see more presence, more equipment, in support of the municipalities" over the next few days, Federal Emergency Management Agency official Alejandro de la Campa told reporters Friday.</div><div class="zn-body__paragraph">• About 3,000 crates of private-sector goods -- such as food meant for grocery stores -- have been sitting idle at the Port of San Juan, in part because not all drivers have reported back to work and also because of other logistical challenges, Gov. Ricardo Rosselló said Friday. </div><div class="zn-body__paragraph">The government will call private owners and ask whether they can pick up the goods. If they cannot, the government will require owners to sell the goods to the Puerto Rican government so that it can deliver them to the people, he said. col-sm-offset-0 col-md-offset-0 col-lg-offset-0 layout"> <div class="moat-trackable pb-f-theme-normal pb-f-dehydrate-false pb-f-async-false full pb-feature pb-layout-item pb-f-article-article-deck" id="article-deck" class="article-deck"> <div class="clear"></div> </div> </div> <div class="moat-trackable pb-f-theme-normal pb-f-dehydrate-false pb-f-async-false full pb-feature pb-layout-item pb-f-article-article-body" moat-id="article/article-body|world" data-chain-name="no-name" data-feature-name="no-name" data-feature-id="article/article-body" data-pb-fingerprint="0f42pbXsipG" id="fIO4D72UtQfEwq"> <div id="article-body" class="article-body"> <div class="pb-sig-line hasnt-headshot has-0-headshots hasnt-bio is-not-column"> <span class="pb-byline" itemprop="author" itemscope href="mailto:herman.wong@washpost.com;rachel.chason@washpost.com?subject=Reader feedback for 'Meet the Air Force general who delivered a powerful speech against racism'"><span class="fa fa-envelope"></span></a></span> <span class="tweet-authors"><span class="pb-twitter-follow unprocessed"><a href="https://twitter.com/@hermanywong" class="twitter-follow-button" data-show-count="false" data-lang="en">Follow @rachel_chason</a></span> </span> <span class="pb-bolt"><i class="fa fa-bolt"></i></span> </div> <article itemprop="articleBody"> <div class="inline-content inline-video"> <div class="posttv-video-embed powa" data-ad-bar="1" data-aspect-ratio="0.5625" data-blurb="1" data-live="0" data-object-id="59cd6669e4b0629cd0bdec93" data-org="wapo" data-playthrough="1" data-uuid="25f8b37c-a492-11e7-b573-8ec86cdfe1ed" data-youtube-id="6TzWW2CXkXc"> <script src="https://d1pz6dax0t5mop.cloudfront.net/prod/PoWaLoaderWapo.js"></script> </div> <div class="inline-video-caption"> <span class="pb-caption">Lt. Gen. Jay Silveria, superintendent of the U.S. Air Force Academy, spoke to cadets and cadet candidates on Sept. 28 after racial slurs were written on the dormitory message boards of five black cadets at the academy's preparatory school. (USAFAOfficial/YouTube)</span> </div> </div> <p>Lt. Gen. Jay Silveria had an important message for U.S. Air Force Academy<strong> </strong>cadets at<strong> </strong>a moment of crisis.</p> <p>Five black cadet candidates at the academy’s preparatory school in Colorado Springs had <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/grade-point/wp/2017/09/28/racial-slurs-written-on-doors-of-five-black-cadet-candidates-at-air-force-academy-preparatory-school/?utm_term=.fb2624ff3dd5">found racial slurs</a> written on the message boards on their doors.</p> <p>Silveria, who took over as the school’s superintendent in August, urged cadets to reach for their phones.</p> <p>“I want you to videotape this so you have it, so you can use it — so that we all have the moral courage together,” he said, surrounded by 1,500 of the academy’s faculty, administrators and athletic coaches.</p> <p>“If you can’t treat someone with dignity and respect, get out.”</p> <p channel="wp.com" class="interstitial-link"> <i> [<a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/investigations/va-chief-took-in-wimbledon-river-cruise-on-european-work-trip/2017/09/29/c1f17046-a458-11e7-8c37-e1d99ad6aa22_story.html?utm_term=.9f3fc3e26653">VA chief took in Wimbledon, river cruise on European work trip; wife’s expenses covered by taxpayers</a>] </i> </p> <p>Silveria’s forceful denunciation has been heard far beyond the walls of the academy in Colorado, introducing the veteran officer to a national audience.</p> <div class="inline-content inline-html"> <blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-width="500"> <p dir="ltr" lang="en">There is only one way to confront hatred and prejudice: head on. Well said, Lt. Gen Silveria. <a href="https://t.co/vQ2Aflo8Tx">https://t.co/vQ2Aflo8Tx</a></p> <p>— Joe Biden (@JoeBiden) <a href="https://twitter.com/JoeBiden/status/913754239272398848?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">September 29, 2017</a></p></blockquote> <p><script async="" charset="utf-8" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script></p> </div> <div class="inline-content inline-html"> <blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-width="500"> <p dir="ltr" lang="en">Important statement by Lt. Gen. Silveria <a href="https://twitter.com/AF_Academy?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">@AF_Academy</a>. I agree, there's no place for racism or bigotry in our military or this great nation. <a href="https://t.co/B5nNlGFmwE">https://t.co/B5nNlGFmwE</a></p> <p>— John McCain (@SenJohnMcCain) <a href="https://twitter.com/SenJohnMcCain/status/913820628662157313?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">September 29, 2017</a></p></blockquote> <p><script async="" charset="utf-8" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js"></script></p> </div> <p>“I wanted to have a direct conversation with them about the power of diversity,” Silveria told CNN’s Brooke Baldwin on Friday, referring to the cadets. “Ultimately, these men and women are going to be lieutenants in the United States Air Force.”</p> <p>Baldwin read Silveria messages of support on Twitter and asked him whether he believed Washington needed better leadership. He replied that his “message to the cadets was not about that.”</p> <p>He said his speech was intended to show the cadets that they were all united “as an institution protecting these values.”</p> <p>Security forces are looking into the matter, according to Lt. Col. Allen Herritage, a spokesman for the U.S. Air Force Academy. The preparatory school is designed for candidates who have shown leadership or other qualities that would make them strong applicants for the academy but who need to shore up their academic work before becoming cadets, Herritage said.</p> <p>Silveria, who graduated from the Air Force Academy in 1985 with a bachelor of science degree, succeeded the academy’s first female superintendent, Lt. Gen. Michelle Johnson.</p> <p>In his 32-year career, Silveria has nearly 4,000 hours of flight time, including combat missions over Iraq and the Balkans, making him one of the Air Force’s most experienced pilots, according to the Colorado Springs <a href="http://gazette.com/ceremony-marks-passing-of-the-torch-to-new-air-force-academy-superintendent/article/1608944">Gazette</a>.</p> <p>“When it came time to pick the next superintendent, Lt. Gen. Jay Silveria was the obvious choice,” Gen. David Goldfein, the branch’s chief of staff, said at Silveria’s appointment ceremony, according to the Gazette. “I don’t believe we have an officer serving in the Air Force today with more combat time, more joint credibility, or more operational understanding of the art of modern war.”</p> <p>Shortly before the ceremony, Silveria, the Air Force Academy’s 20th superintendent, was promoted from major general to lieutenant general, the rank required for the position, the Gazette reported.</p> <p>He was previously deputy commander of U.S. <a href="http://www.military.com/air-force">Air Forces</a> Central Command and deputy commander of Central Command’s Combined Forces Air Component in southwest Asia, according to <a href="http://www.military.com/daily-news/2017/05/18/1985-air-force-academy-graduate-appointed-school-leader.html">Military.com</a>.</p> <p>On Twitter, Silveria has been widely praised for his leadership, with some suggesting he should run for office one day.</p> <div class="inline-content inline-html"> <blockquote class="twitter-tweet" data-width="500"> <p dir="ltr" lang="en">This is what power, leadership, and advocacy looks like…. class="lower-container" data-reactid="17"><div class="TwoColumnLayout_container_385r0 inner TwoColumnLayout_fluid-left_3DYLH" data-reactid="18"><div class="TwoColumnLayout_column_1uZPg class="BylineBar_border-wrap_2Jm9i" data-reactid="22"><p class="BylineBar_byline_31BCV" data-reactid="23">Reuters Staff</p><div class="BylineBar_last-container_1J6-E" data-reactid="24"><p class="LazyImage_container_1Z7A0" style="background-image:none;" data-reactid="34"><div class="LazyImage_image_1KsYy LazyImage_fallback_2kFne" speaking as he makes a statement in Baghdad, Iraq September 24, 2017. REUTERS/via Reuters TV</span></figcaption></div></div><div class="ArticleBody_body_2ECha" data-reactid="38"><p data-reactid="39">BAGHDAD (Reuters) - Iraqi Prime Minister Haider al-Abadi said on Saturday an invitation from French President Emmanuel Macron to visit Paris was not related to the Kurdish independence referendum. </p><p data-reactid="40">The invitation was delivered to Abadi on Aug. 26 by the French foreign and defense ministers during a visit to Baghdad, Abadi&rsquo;s office said in a statement, adding its purpose was &ldquo;to strengthen bilateral relations and concentrate efforts on fighting terrorism.&rdquo; </p><p data-reactid="41">A source in Macron&rsquo;s office said Abadi had accepted an invitation from Macron to visit Paris on Oct. 5 for talks on the Kurdish independence referendum. </p><p data-reactid="42">A phone call between Abadi and Macron, after Monday&rsquo;s referendum &ldquo;did not mention in any way the need to recognize the rights of the Kurdish people,&rdquo; said Abadi&rsquo;s statement.  </p><div data-reactid="43"></div><div class="Attribution_attribution_o4ojT" data-reactid="44"><p class="Attribution_content_27_rw" data-reactid="45">Reporting by Maher Chmaytelli; Editing by Janet Lawrence</p></div><div class="ArticleBody_trustBadgeContainer_1_iEv" data-reactid="46"><span class="ArticleBody_trustBadgeTitle_3xFqc"
